<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="189" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/68-1024x189.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2209" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/68-1024x189.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/68-300x55.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/68-768x142.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/68.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 68</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Here is the newly created scheduled task in Windows Task Scheduler:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="289" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/69-1024x289.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2210" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/69-1024x289.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/69-300x85.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/69-768x216.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/69.jpg 1366w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 69</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The ransomware launches itself with the following parameters &#8220;&#8211;Admin IsNotAutoStart IsNotTask&#8221; (IsNotAutoStart = malware didn&#8217;t run based on the Run registry key,  IsNotTask = malware didn&#8217;t run based on the scheduled task):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="287" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/70-1024x287.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2212" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/70-1024x287.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/70-300x84.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/70-768x215.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/70.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 70</figcaption></figure></div>



<p><strong>&#8220;&#8211;Task</strong>&#8220;<strong> parameter</strong></p>



<p>We&#8217;ll only highlight different actions that are performed by the ransomware running with this parameter without mentioning the same actions as in the case of running with no parameters. </p>



<p>GetAdaptersInfo&nbsp;is utilized to retrieve adapter information (including the MAC address) for the localhost:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="143" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/71-1024x143.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2218" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/71-1024x143.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/71-300x42.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/71-768x107.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/71.jpg 1166w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 71</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The malware calls the CryptAcquireContextW API in order to obtain a handle to a particular key container within a cryptographic service provider (0x1 = <strong>PROV_RSA_FULL</strong> and 0xF0000000 = <strong>CRYPT_VERIFYCONTEXT</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="188" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/72-1024x188.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2219" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/72-1024x188.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/72-300x55.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/72-768x141.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/72.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 72</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The binary creates a handle to a CSP hash object using the CryptCreateHash API (0x8003 = <strong>CALG_MD5</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="171" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/73-1024x171.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2220" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/73-1024x171.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/73-300x50.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/73-768x128.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/73.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 73</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The ransomware hashes a buffer that contains the MAC address extracted above via a function call to CryptHashData:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="159" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/74-1024x159.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2221" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/74-1024x159.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/74-300x47.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/74-768x120.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/74.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 74</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The MD5 hash value is extracted by calling the CryptGetHashParam&nbsp;routine (0x2 = <strong>HP_HASHVAL</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="191" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/75-1024x191.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2222" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/75-1024x191.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/75-300x56.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/75-768x143.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/75.jpg 1165w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 75</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>A new thread is created by calling the CreateThread API:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="218" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/76-1024x218.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2223" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/76-1024x218.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/76-300x64.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/76-768x164.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/76.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 76</figcaption></figure></div>



<p><strong>Thread activity – sub_16E690</strong></p>



<p>The RegOpenKeyExW function is used to open the &#8220;Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion&#8221; registry key (0x80000001 = <strong>HKEY_CURRENT_USER&nbsp;</strong>and 0xF003F = <strong>KEY_ALL_ACCESS</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="215" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/77-1024x215.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2224" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/77-1024x215.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/77-300x63.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/77-768x162.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/77.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 77</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The process is looking for a value named &#8220;SysHelper&#8221;, which doesn&#8217;t exist at this time (this is different from the one in figure 34):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="228" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/78-1024x228.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2227" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/78-1024x228.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/78-300x67.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/78-768x171.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/78.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 78</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The entry from above is created, and its value is set to 1 using the RegSetValueExW API:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="208" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/79-1024x208.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2228" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/79-1024x208.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/79-300x61.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/79-768x156.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/79.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 79</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The executable tries to locate a file called &#8220;bowsakkdestx.txt&#8221; in the &#8220;C:\Users\&lt;User&gt;\AppData\Local&#8221; directory, which doesn&#8217;t exist on our machine:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="121" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/80-1024x121.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2229" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/80-1024x121.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/80-300x35.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/80-768x91.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/80.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 80</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>There is a function call to InternetOpenW similar to the one presented in figure 23 (with the same user agent). The binary performs a GET request to the C2 server securebiz[.]org with the parameter pid = MD5(MAC address):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="271" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/81-1024x271.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2232" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/81-1024x271.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/81-300x80.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/81-768x204.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/81.jpg 1166w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 81</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The response from the server is read using the InternetReadFile function:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="159" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/82-1024x159.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2233" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/82-1024x159.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/82-300x47.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/82-768x120.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/82.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 82</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The binary creates the file called &#8220;bowsakkdestx.txt&#8221; using fopen:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="138" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/83-1024x138.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2234" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/83-1024x138.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/83-300x40.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/83-768x103.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/83.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 83</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The file is populated using a function call to fwrite (the C2 server was down during our analysis, so we emulated the network communications using FakeNet):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="165" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/84-1024x165.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2235" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/84-1024x165.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/84-300x48.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/84-768x124.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/84.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 84</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>An example of a real response can be seen at <a href="https://app.any.run/tasks/900f626a-2bf6-48b2-85f9-2328f2b2d0d2/">https://app.any.run/tasks/900f626a-2bf6-48b2-85f9-2328f2b2d0d2/</a> and contains 2 elements: &#8220;public_key&#8221; and &#8220;id&#8221;. The malware wants to extract the &#8220;public_key&#8221; value from the response:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="167" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/85-1024x167.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2236" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/85-1024x167.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/85-300x49.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/85-768x125.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/85.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 85</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Even though the C2 server was down, the binary comes with a hard-coded RSA public key. The file from above is deleted in any case:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="98" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/86-1024x98.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2237" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/86-1024x98.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/86-300x29.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/86-768x74.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/86.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 86</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Using multiple XOR operations with 0x80, the ransomware decrypts the RSA public key in PKCS1 format, a victim ID, and a URL that leads to another malicious file at http[:]//securebiz[.]org/files/1/build3.exe:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="816" height="663" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/87.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2238" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/87.jpg 816w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/87-300x244.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/87-768x624.jpg 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 816px) 100vw, 816px" /><figcaption>Figure 87</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>We continue to analyze the main thread. A mutex called &#8220;{1D6FC66E-D1F3-422C-8A53-C0BBCF3D900D}&#8221; is created via a function call to CreateMutexA:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="133" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/88-1024x133.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2241" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/88-1024x133.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/88-300x39.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/88-768x100.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/88.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 88</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The malware decrypts the ransom note using the XOR operator:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="816" height="278" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/89.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2243" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/89.jpg 816w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/89-300x102.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/89-768x262.jpg 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 816px) 100vw, 816px" /><figcaption>Figure 89</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The following information is also decrypted (a list of files to be skipped, a list of extensions to be skipped, and a list of directories to be skipped):</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>ntuser.dat, ntuser.dat.LOG1, ntuser.dat.LOG2, ntuser.pol</li><li>.sys, .ini, .DLL, .dll, .blf, .bat, .lnk, .regtrans-ms</li><li>C:\SystemID\, C:\Users\Default User\, C:\Users\Public\, C:\Users\All Users\, C:\Users\Default\, C:\Documents and Settings\, C:\ProgramData\, C:\Recovery\, C:\System Volume Information\, C:\Users\%username%\A&#8221;ppData\Roaming\, C:\Users\%username%\AppData\Local\, C:\Windows\, C:\PerfLogs\, C:\ProgramData\Microsoft\, C:\ProgramData\Package Cache\, C:\Users\Public\, C:\$Recycle.Bin\, C:\$WINDOWS.~BT\, C:\dell\, C:\Intel\, C:\MSOCache\, C:\Program Files\, C:\Program Files (x86)\, C:\Games\, C:\Windows.old\</li><li>D:\Users\%username%\AppData\Roaming\, D:\Users\%username%\AppData\Local\, D:\Windows\, D:\PerfLogs\, D:\ProgramData\Desktop\, D:\ProgramData\Microsoft\, D:\ProgramData\Package Cache\, D:\Users\Public\, D:\$Recycle.Bin\, D:\$WINDOWS.~BT\, D:\dell\, D:\Intel\, D:\MSOCache\, D:\Program Files\, D:\Program Files (x86)\, D:\Games\</li><li>E:\Users\%username%\AppData\Roaming\, E:\Users\%username%\AppData\Local\, E:\Windows\, E:\PerfLogs\, E:\ProgramData\Desktop\, E:\ProgramData\Microsoft\, E:\ProgramData\Package Cache\, E:\Users\Public\, E:\$Recycle.Bin\, E:\$WINDOWS.~BT\, E:\dell\, E:\Intel\, E:\MSOCache\, E:\Program Files\, E:\Program Files (x86)\, E:\Games\</li><li>F:\Users\%username%\AppData\Roaming\, F:\Users\%username%\AppData\Local\, F:\Windows\, F:\PerfLogs\, F:\ProgramData\Desktop\, F:\ProgramData\Microsoft\, F:\Users\Public\, F:\$Recycle.Bin\, F:\$WINDOWS.~BT\, F:\dell\, F:\Intel\</li></ul>



<p>The executable retrieves the user name associated with the current thread by calling the GetUserNameW API:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="125" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/90-1024x125.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2248" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/90-1024x125.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/90-300x37.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/90-768x94.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/90.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 90</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The malicious process is looking for a file called &#8220;PersonalID.txt&#8221; that doesn&#8217;t exist at this time:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="149" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/91-1024x149.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2250" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/91-1024x149.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/91-300x44.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/91-768x112.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/91.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 91</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>CreateDirectoryW is utilized to create a directory called &#8220;C:\SystemID&#8221;:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="114" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/92-1024x114.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2251" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/92-1024x114.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/92-300x33.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/92-768x85.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/92.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 92</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The ransomware creates the file &#8220;C:\SystemID\PersonalID.txt&#8221; and writes the victim ID to it:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="176" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/93-1024x176.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2252" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/93-1024x176.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/93-300x52.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/93-768x132.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/93.jpg 1172w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 93</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>It&#8217;s very uncommon that the malware searches the system for a file called &#8220;I:\5d2860c89d774.jpg&#8221; (0xC0000000 = <strong>GENERIC_READ</strong> | <strong>GENERIC_WRITE</strong>, 0x1 = <strong>FILE_SHARE_READ</strong>, 0x3 = <strong><strong>OPEN_EXISTING</strong></strong> and 0x80 = <strong>FILE_ATTRIBUTE_NORMAL</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="256" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/94-1024x256.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2253" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/94-1024x256.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/94-300x75.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/94-768x192.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/94.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 94</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>LoadCursorW&nbsp;is used to load the standard arrow resource from the executable (0x7F00 = <strong>IDC_ARROW</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="179" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/95-1024x179.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2254" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/95-1024x179.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/95-300x53.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/95-768x135.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/95.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 95</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The binary registers a window class using the RegisterClassExW&nbsp;routine:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="187" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/96-1024x187.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2257" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/96-1024x187.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/96-300x55.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/96-768x140.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/96.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 96</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>CreateWindowExW is utilized to create a new window called &#8220;LPCWSTRszTitle&#8221; (0xCF0000 =&nbsp;<strong>WS_OVERLAPPEDWINDOW</strong> and 0x80000000 =&nbsp;<strong>CW_USEDEFAULT</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="324" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/97-1024x324.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2258" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/97-1024x324.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/97-300x95.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/97-768x243.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/97.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 97</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The window created earlier is hided by calling the ShowWindow&nbsp;routine (0x0 = <strong>SW_HIDE</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="113" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/99-1-1024x113.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2264" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/99-1-1024x113.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/99-1-300x33.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/99-1-768x85.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/99-1.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 98</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>We need to analyze the window procedure defined in figure 96 (sub_16BAE0).</p>



<p>The malware uses the ntdllDefWindowProcW API in order to call the default window procedure whenever a particular message needs to be processed (0x24 = <strong>WM_GETMINMAXINFO</strong>, 0x81 = <strong>WM_NCCREATE</strong>, 0x83 = <strong>WM_NCCALCSIZE</strong>&nbsp;and 0x1 = <strong>WM_CREATE</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="614" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/98-1024x614.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2259" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/98-1024x614.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/98-300x180.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/98-768x461.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/98.jpg 1165w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 99</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>GetLogicalDrives&nbsp;is used to retrieve a bitmask that represents the available disk drives:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="9" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/100-1-1024x9.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2267" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/100-1-1024x9.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/100-1-300x3.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/100-1-768x6.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/100-1.jpg 1199w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 100</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The ransomware forces the system not to display the critical-error message box and sending these errors to the calling process (0x1 = <strong>SEM_FAILCRITICALERRORS</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="94" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/101-1024x94.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2270" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/101-1024x94.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/101-300x27.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/101-768x70.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/101.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 101</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The file extracts the type of the drives by calling the GetDriveTypeA API and compares it with 2 (<strong>DRIVE_REMOVABLE</strong>), 3 (<strong>DRIVE_FIXED</strong>), 4 (<strong>DRIVE_REMOTE</strong>) and 6 (<strong>DRIVE_RAMDISK</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="294" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/102-2-1024x294.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2278" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/102-2-1024x294.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/102-2-300x86.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/102-2-768x220.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/102-2.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 102</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Two new threads are created using the CreateThread function:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="192" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/103-1024x192.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2275" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/103-1024x192.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/103-300x56.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/103-768x144.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/103.jpg 1171w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 103</figcaption></figure></div>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="190" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/104-1024x190.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2276" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/104-1024x190.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/104-300x56.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/104-768x143.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/104.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 104</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The file retrieves a message from the message queue by calling the GetMessageW routine, translates virtual-key messages into character messages using TranslateMessage, and finally dispatches a message to a window procedure using DispatchMessageW:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="153" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/105-1024x153.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2280" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/105-1024x153.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/105-300x45.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/105-768x115.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/105.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 105</figcaption></figure></div>



<p><strong>Thread activity – sub_16FD80</strong></p>



<p>The malware enumerates all resources on the network via a function call to WNetOpenEnumW (0x2 = <strong>RESOURCE_GLOBALNET</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="193" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/106-1024x193.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2281" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/106-1024x193.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/106-300x56.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/106-768x144.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/106.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 106</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>WNetEnumResourceW is utilized to further enumerate the network resources:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="256" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/107-1024x256.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2282" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/107-1024x256.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/107-300x75.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/107-768x192.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/107.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 107</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The message <strong>DBT_DEVICEREMOVECOMPLETE</strong> (&#8220;A device or piece of media has been removed&#8221;) is sent to the window created earlier, and its procedure will handle it:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="161" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/108-1024x161.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2283" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/108-1024x161.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/108-300x47.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/108-768x121.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/108.jpg 1167w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 108</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>When the window procedure receives the message, it calls the GetComputerNameW API in order to get the NetBIOS name of the local machine:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="113" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/109-1024x113.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2284" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/109-1024x113.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/109-300x33.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/109-768x85.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/109.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 109</figcaption></figure></div>



<p><strong>Thread activity – sub_16F130</strong></p>



<p>The ransomware creates the ransom note called &#8220;_readme.txt&#8221; in every directory that it encrypts:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="251" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/110-1024x251.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2286" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/110-1024x251.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/110-300x74.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/110-768x189.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/110.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 110</figcaption></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="186" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/111-1024x186.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2287" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/111-1024x186.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/111-300x54.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/111-768x139.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/111.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 111</figcaption></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="414" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/112-1024x414.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2289" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/112-1024x414.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/112-300x121.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/112-768x311.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/112.jpg 1061w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 112</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The files are enumerated using the FindFirstFileW and FindNextFileW APIs:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="229" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/113-1024x229.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2291" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/113-1024x229.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/113-300x67.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/113-768x172.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/113.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 113</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The directories mentioned under figure 89 will not be encrypted. The file extension is extracted by calling the PathFindExtensionW routine:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="93" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/114-1024x93.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2293" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/114-1024x93.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/114-300x27.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/114-768x70.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/114.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 114</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The files and file extensions mentioned under figure 89 will be skipped. The ransomware also avoids files that have the &#8220;.tisc&#8221; extension because this will be appended after the encryption is complete:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="342" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/115-1024x342.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2295" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/115-1024x342.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/115-300x100.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/115-768x256.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/115.jpg 1166w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 115</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Each targeted file is opened using the CreateFileW routine:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="255" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/116-1024x255.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2297" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/116-1024x255.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/116-300x75.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/116-768x191.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/116.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 116</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The file content is read by calling the ReadFile function:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="213" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/117-1024x213.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2300" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/117-1024x213.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/117-300x62.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/117-768x160.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/117.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 117</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>There is a function call to CryptAcquireContextW (as in figure 72) and another one to CryptCreateHash (as in figure 73). The malware hashes a buffer that contains the first 5 bytes from the targeted file and the RSA public key, as shown in figure 118:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="186" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/118-1024x186.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2303" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/118-1024x186.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/118-300x55.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/118-768x140.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/118.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 118</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The MD5 hash value is extracted by calling the CryptGetHashParam&nbsp;routine (0x2 =&nbsp;<strong>HP_HASHVAL</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="192" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/119-1024x192.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2304" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/119-1024x192.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/119-300x56.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/119-768x144.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/119.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 119</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The binary creates a new UUID (16 random bytes) by calling the UuidCreate API (which internally uses CryptGenRandom):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="128" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/120-1024x128.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2307" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/120-1024x128.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/120-300x37.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/120-768x96.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/120.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 120</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The process converts the UUID to a string using the UuidToStringA&nbsp;API:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="164" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/121-1024x164.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2310" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/121-1024x164.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/121-300x48.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/121-768x123.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/121.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 121</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Based on the value generated above, the ransomware constructs the following Salsa20 matrix:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="520" height="60" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/122.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2311" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/122.jpg 520w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/122-300x35.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 520px) 100vw, 520px" /><figcaption>Figure 122</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>A snippet of the Salsa20 algorithm implemented by the malware is presented below:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="389" height="664" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/123.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2313" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/123.jpg 389w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/123-176x300.jpg 176w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 389px) 100vw, 389px" /><figcaption>Figure 123</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The process encrypts the file content using the Salsa20 algorithm, however the first 5 bytes from the targeted file are not encrypted. Based on the strings presented in figure 124 and our analysis of the RSA implementation, we believe that the malware developers have included the OpenSSL code found at <a href="https://github.com/openssl/openssl">https://github.com/openssl/openssl</a> (or similar code taken from other projects):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="582" height="600" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/124.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2314" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/124.jpg 582w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/124-291x300.jpg 291w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 582px) 100vw, 582px" /><figcaption>Figure 124</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The binary encrypts the UUID generated before using the RSA public key embedded in the file:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="356" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/125-1024x356.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2317" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/125-1024x356.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/125-300x104.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/125-768x267.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/125.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 125</figcaption></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="180" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/126-1024x180.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2320" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/126-1024x180.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/126-300x53.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/126-768x135.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/126.jpg 1167w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 126</figcaption></figure></div>

<p>The encrypted file has the following structure that highlights different elements:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="619" height="406" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/131.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2326" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/131.jpg 619w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/131-300x197.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 619px) 100vw, 619px" /><figcaption>Figure 131</figcaption></figure></div>



<p><strong>&#8220;&#8211;AutoStart</strong>&#8220;<strong>&nbsp;parameter</strong></p>



<p>The activity is similar to the case discussed above.</p>



<p><strong>&#8220;&#8211;Admin IsNotAutoStart IsNotTask</strong>&#8220;<strong>&nbsp;parameters</strong></p>



<p>The binary establishes a connection to the service control manager by calling the OpenSCManagerW routine (0x1 = <strong>SC_MANAGER_CONNECT</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="134" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/132-1024x134.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2329" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/132-1024x134.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/132-300x39.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/132-768x101.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/132.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 132</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>A service called &#8220;MYSQL&#8221; is opened by the process via a function call to OpenServiceW (0x20 = <strong>SERVICE_STOP</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1169" height="152" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/133-1024x133.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2330" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/133-1024x133.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/133-300x39.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/133-768x100.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/133.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1169px) 100vw, 1169px" /><figcaption>Figure 133</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Whether the service would exist on a host, the ransomware would stop it using the ControlService API:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="422" height="309" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/134.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2331" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/134.jpg 422w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/134-300x220.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 422px) 100vw, 422px" /><figcaption>Figure 134</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The file decrypts another URL that will be used to download more malicious files, http[:]//znpst[.]top/dl/build2.exe:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="522" height="72" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/135.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2332" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/135.jpg 522w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/135-300x41.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 522px) 100vw, 522px" /><figcaption>Figure 135</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>A new thread is created by calling the CreateThread function:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="208" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/136-1024x208.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2333" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/136-1024x208.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/136-300x61.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/136-768x156.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/136.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 136</figcaption></figure></div>



<p><strong>Thread activity – StartAddress</strong> (<strong>sub_16DBD0</strong>)</p>



<p>UuidCreate is utilized to generate a new UUID:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="118" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/137-1024x118.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2335" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/137-1024x118.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/137-300x35.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/137-768x89.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/137.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 137</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The UuidToStringA&nbsp;routine is used to convert the UUID to a string:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="162" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/138-1024x162.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2336" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/138-1024x162.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/138-300x47.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/138-768x122.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/138.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 138</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The malicious process creates a new directory based on the UUID generated above:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="165" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/139-1024x165.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2341" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/139-1024x165.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/139-300x48.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/139-768x124.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/139.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 139</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The binary performs a GET request to http[:]//znpst[.]top/dl/build2.exe using InternetOpenUrlA:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="150" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/140-1024x150.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2343" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/140-1024x150.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/140-300x44.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/140-768x113.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/140.jpg 1171w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 140</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>According to the analysis from <a href="https://any.run/report/cd6bf2f554a9aa446cb36d28e374e1010268cbda8f55eb0043fbe6e2724128be/152e55c2-5e8f-4fe2-a764-7876ba00f03e">https://any.run/report/cd6bf2f554a9aa446cb36d28e374e1010268cbda8f55eb0043fbe6e2724128be/152e55c2-5e8f-4fe2-a764-7876ba00f03e</a>, the above executable is a malware called Ursnif (banking Trojan). </p>



<p>The status code is extracted by calling the HttpQueryInfoW routine (0x20000013 = <strong>HTTP_QUERY_FLAG_NUMBER</strong> | <strong>HTTP_QUERY_STATUS_CODE</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="208" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/141-1024x208.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2345" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/141-1024x208.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/141-300x61.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/141-768x156.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/141.jpg 1171w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 141</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>A file called &#8220;build2.exe&#8221; is created in the new directory:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="233" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/142-1024x233.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2348" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/142-1024x233.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/142-300x68.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/142-768x175.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/142.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 142</figcaption></figure></div>

<p>According to multiple online resources, the above file is supposed to be an infamous info-stealer called Vidar. The process of reading data from the server, creating the malicious file, etc. is the same as above and isn&#8217;t explained again.</p>



<p>For completeness, we will also provide details about the other parameters that can be used, as displayed at <a href="https://app.any.run/tasks/635cd7df-e4b7-4d1a-a937-e8d8599e6c72/">https://app.any.run/tasks/635cd7df-e4b7-4d1a-a937-e8d8599e6c72/</a>. </p>



<p><strong>&#8220;&#8211;ForNetRes &#8220;jwvfPPgZoQyg6Q6he8weP7iDsH9FKc74ICjysAt2&#8243; r77yXePcnmrctJPWrZCcbJgUlAtOa1FC9Na710t1 IsNotAutoStart IsNotTask&#8221; parameters</strong></p>



<p>The binary creates a mutex called &#8220;{FBB4BCC6-05C7-4ADD-B67B-A98A697323C1}&#8221; using the CreateMutexA API:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="132" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/147-1024x132.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2360" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/147-1024x132.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/147-300x39.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/147-768x99.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/147.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 147</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>According to online sources, the first parameter can be considered as a Key and the second one as a Personal ID. The malware performs a hashing operation (MD5) on the Key:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="170" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/148-1024x170.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2362" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/148-1024x170.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/148-300x50.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/148-768x128.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/148.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 148</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The hash value is extracted using the CryptGetHashParam function (0x2 = <strong>HP_HASHVAL</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="191" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/149-1024x191.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2363" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/149-1024x191.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/149-300x56.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/149-768x143.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/149.jpg 1170w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 149</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The execution flow is similar to the one starting with figure 90 and will not be reiterated.</p>



<p>&#8220;<strong>&#8211;Service 4904 &#8220;jwvfPPgZoQyg6Q6he8weP7iDsH9FKc74ICjysAt2&#8221;</strong> <strong>r77yXePcnmrctJPWrZCcbJgUlAtOa1FC9Na710t1</strong>&#8221; <strong>parameters</strong></p>



<p>The above value represents the parent process ID, which is converted from string to a long integer value:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="130" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/150-1024x130.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2366" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/150-1024x130.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/150-300x38.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/150-768x97.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/150.jpg 1168w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 150</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The ransomware opens the local process object using the OpenProcess routine (0x100000 = <strong>SYNCHRONIZE</strong>):</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="131" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/151-1024x131.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2367" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/151-1024x131.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/151-300x38.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/151-768x98.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/151.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 151</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>After the parent process enters the signaled state, the file dispatches incoming sent messages, checks for posted messages, and then retrieves the messages:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="170" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/152-1024x170.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2368" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/152-1024x170.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/152-300x50.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/152-768x127.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/152.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 152</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>The malicious binary retrieves the exit code of the current process and then kills itself using TerminateProcess:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="396" height="153" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/153.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2369" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/153.jpg 396w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/153-300x116.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 396px) 100vw, 396px" /><figcaption>Figure 153</figcaption></figure></div>



<p>Finally, we describe the case when the country code belongs to the following list: &#8220;RU&#8221;, &#8220;BY&#8221;, &#8220;UA&#8221;, &#8220;AZ&#8221;, &#8220;AM&#8221;, &#8220;TJ&#8221;, &#8220;KZ&#8221;, &#8220;KG&#8221;, &#8220;UZ&#8221; and &#8220;SY&#8221;. </p>



<p>CreateMutexA is utilized to create a mutex called &#8220;{FBB4BCC6-05C7-4ADD-B67B-A98A697323C1}&#8221;:</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="130" src="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/154-1024x130.jpg" alt="" class="wp-image-2372" srcset="https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/154-1024x130.jpg 1024w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/154-300x38.jpg 300w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/154-768x97.jpg 768w, https://cybergeeks.tech/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/154.jpg 1169w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption>Figure 154</figcaption></figure></div>

<p style="font-size:25px">INDICATORS OF COMPROMISE</p>



<p>C2 domains: </p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>securebiz[.]org  </li></ul>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>znpst[.]top</li></ul>



<p>SHA256: 4380c45fd46d1a63cffe4d37cf33b0710330a766b7700af86020a936cdd09cbe</p>



<p>Scheduled Task: &#8220;Time Trigger Task&#8221;</p>



<p>Registry key: HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run\SysHelper</p>



<p>User-agent: &#8220;Microsoft Internet Explorer&#8221;</p>



<p>PDB paths: </p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>“C:\xudihiguhe\jegovicatusoca\jijetogez\winucet\xusev\kucor.pdb”  </li><li>“e:\doc\my work (c++)_git\encryption\release\encrypt_win_api.pdb”</li></ul>



<p>URLs: </p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>http[:]//securebiz[.]org/fhsgtsspen6/get.php   </li><li>http[:]//securebiz.org/files/1/build3.exe   </li><li>http[:]//znpst.top/dl/build2.exe</li><li>https[:]//api.2ip.ua/geo.json</li></ul>
